text:
OMG I don't even know where to begin.  The most delicious thing I've ever put into my mouth!  Like lots of others, I boiled the ribs (I used baby-backs) for 45 minutes.  Then, as instructed, I placed on a pan, covered with barbeque sauce (I used Sweet Baby Rays), covered with foil and cooked at 325 for an hour.  After that, I removed the foil, turned up the oven to 400, and slathered more barbeque sauce on, then cooked uncovered x 10 minutes.  Removed from oven and let rest around 10 minutes.  Folks, this could win an award :)

You can try the fancy rubs with it, but for most folks that just isn't necessary. I really love  this method.  The day before cooking I do a brown sugar rub and put the ribs in their foil pouches.  The next morning they go right to the oven from the fridge.  At  the two hour mark I open them up and brush them with my sauce and give them thirty minutes.  Then I turn  them and brush another layer of sauce and another thirty minutes.  Done!   Tender, moist, fall off the bone, delicious and easy cleanup.

BEST DINNER IN A LONG TIME!  OMG THESE RIBS ARE SO GOOD. I put the dry rub for ribs by Denise (found on this website)  on my ribs for approximately 24 hours (I put them into a plastic bag.). Then  I covered them tightly in Tin foil. I put them into the oven at 300 degrees for  2 hours. I  let them cool for approximately 1 hour then put them on my green egg (at 400 degrees) for 3 minutes/side. I served them with warmed Sweet  baby Rays barbecue sauce.  I made Chef Johns macaroni salad and fresh kale salad. Not one rib or side dish was left I got 10s from all of my guests. So sweet !

I followed a previous review and did a dry rub instead of the bbq sauce. My dry rub consisted of brown sugar, cayenne pepper, natures seasoning, smoked paprika and chopped garlic. I marinated it overnight wrapped tight in foil then baked at 300 for 2 hrs and 40min. Removed the foil and brushed with bbq, turned the oven on broil and broiled the ribs for about 5min. These ribs were sooooo tender and flavorful! I used to boil ribs before placing them in the oven or grill, never again! This is my go to, so much easier and the ribs taste soooo much better!

These turned out really well. Haven't had a lot of success with ribs until this recipe. Tweaked it a little. Used the dry rub recipe found here. Then was unsure what to do, so I borrowed. Wrapped in foil, put on a rack, and baked at 225 for about 3.5 hrs. Then unwrapped and used convection roast feature in oven. Convection temp was 275 for the final hour. Then put BBQ sauce on and broiled  until sauce carmelized. Monitored so they wouldn't turn to charcoal. Let them sit for about 10 minutes wrapped in foil. Turned out excellent. This is a great recipe

I'm only giving 4 stars because I used most of the method, not the ingredients as written. I only had about 1 1/4 lbs. of back ribs for just me. Using reviewer Cathy M.'s recipe (wow, 10 years ago!) I made a rub of 2T. brown sugar, 2t. paprika, 1t black pepper, 1t kosher salt, 1/8t each garlic powder and onion powder, and a pinch of cayenne. I cut the rack in half and rubbed each half well, wrapped them in foil, and put them in a bowl and in the refrig. The next day at dinner time, I made up my own bbq sauce with what I had in the house.

text:
Best ribs ever!! Made about 4 lbs. of baby back ribs already cut into individual pieces with membrain removed. Made some changes. Used rub as suggested by Cathy  M. review for this recipe. Rub ribs & wrap tightly in foil. Place  in plastic bag in fridge to prevent leakage   Marinate ribs overnight with rub and baked with rub only. Baked foil packets on cookie sheet in oven  @ 300 for about 2 hours & 15 minutes. Let them sit for about half hour while preparing rest of meal. Lastly placed ribs on Pam sprayed foil lined baking sheet. Brushed them with Baby Rays original BBQ sauce ( our favorite ) and placed under low broiler for about 3 - 4 minutes on each side until carmelized. Tender & Delish!!!  First time ever to review a recipe. Had to because I was thrilled about how great they turned out. Love allrecipes.com.

text:
I've used this recipe a few times and each time the ribs are tender, juicy and fall off the bone. A very easy way to remove the membrane is to take a butter knife,work it under the membrane at one end once you have enough to get a good grip on the membrane use pull it off. This will help to make them a little more tender. Also, if cooking these on your grill, place the foil with the bone on the grates; this will prevent the meat side from getting over cooked. I also move the ribs from the foil and brush fresh bb que sauce and return to the grill for 5 minutes on each side.

userID:
7116609
Display Name:
Stock Piler
isPro:

photo:
https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/5614248.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
I modified this recipe quite a bit, since it is a base and I couldnt find my original recipe. Actually used bits of several recipes from the site.
For marination, I basted the ribs with liquid smoke,  worcestershire and apple sauce. Then used 2 packs of Grill Mates marinade packs (very spicy) for a dry rub and marinated overnight in foil.
I didnt use any pre-made barbeque sauce. Instead I made my own using the Applesauce Barbeque Sauce recipe from this site and excluded the lemon juice since I didnt have any.
Took the ribs out of fridge for an hour and then cooked theM in the oven at 225 for 3 hours. Turned up to 250, basted and cooked for 15 minutes on each side. Got internal temp to 140. They did fall off the bone. One piece fell on the floor as I turned it over, so I was required to eat those, per kid demand. The 5 second rule applied here. Took them out and set the broiler (550), basted and put them in for 5 minutes. Basted again and turned over, broiling for another 5 minutesBroiling makes the sauce stick to the ribs. The spicy dry rub and the sweet sauce gives the ribs a moderately sweet and spicy taste without either overpowering.
Delicioso! I have the pickiest ADHD kids in the world and they devoured a whole slab by themselves, quietly!

text:
I do my ribs a little different. I never wrap them when cooking. I rub them and refrigerate over night. Line a baking sheet with foil and oil down a little. Bake them a half hour at 300 degrees.lower oven to 250 degrees. load ribs up with sweet baby rays sauce you don't want to see the meat. Bake for about 3 to 3 1/2 hours loading more sauce on every half hour or so. I have been doing them this way for years. I bring these to many functions, they call me the rib man.

text:
I made these for my girlfriend and she claims they are the best ribs she's ever had. I did include Cathy M.'s famous rub on the ribs. They turned out quite spicy and the broil with the sauce makes them sticky, neither of which I like, but both of which my girlfriend loves, so that means I'll be making them her way every time. They turn out super tender, in fact her only complaint is that they actually fall off the bone to the point where you grab a rib and pull and all you get is bone. My friend joked about this being how they make the McRibs without any ribs. I've tried without marinating in advance and the flavor just doesn't sink in very well, but delicious nonetheless. On some occasions I've also used the more cost affordable spare ribs instead of baby backs and they still turn out great without any change in the recipe. This has become one of my staple recipes when I'm looking to impress someone.

there isnt really a recipe for bbq sauce for these ribs.  but thanks for the instructions on how to cook it.  i did however find a recipie for a jack Daniels bbq sauce from their website and cooked the ribs kinda like this recipe. i didnt wrap it in the foil, that just took way to long and really didnt care for it. i marinaded it over nite with some montreal chicken spice and the JD sauce  baked it in a pan for 2.5 hours made more sauce and brushed it on the ribs while broiling it in the oven for about 15 minutes. watch very carefully when doing this.. i had a couple casualties.  i fed 2 hungry men and myself this way and we had the "econo-sized" pack of ribs. there was no left overs at all.  thanks for the reviews everyone.. it definitely helped.

text:
I have thought long and hard about how to best described this recipe.  I personnaly used the BBQ Dry Rub found on this site but halve the salt (I truly love salt but found it to be too salty). I removed the membrane on the back of the ribs for extra tenderness.  I used my favourite BBQ sauce which after many different kinds and attempts, found the PC Chipotle and Beer to be the best.  For the rest, I followed the recipe to the T and everyone I have serve it to just goes crazy for it.  My ribs became famous through my circle of friends and even though I was tempted to take the credit, I made sure to give credit to this site.    I considered putting them on the BBQ for a few minutes but didn't see the point.  Why change something that is perfect.  If you find the sauce too runny after cooking, simply take them out of the package and put them into a Pyrex bowl and add a bit of BBQ sauce for extra stickyness...  Lastly, I served the ribs with the recipe Sangria Sangria from this site and Oh Mama Mia!!!  MMMmmmmm

I agree with JED901. This is more of a method, than a recipe....but a great method that can be used in many ways. I prepared 3 racks for the 4th of July (yesterday)...my first time using this "method". I first just cut the membrane on the back between each bone (much easier);then wrapped each 1/2 rack in heavy foil with a little beer, some white onion pieces and Old Country Deli "Rib Round UP" (only available on line. Baked in oven at 300 for 3 hours. Brushed on Rays BBQ sauce (lightly) and  put on BBQ for 5 minutes each.  They disappeared upon serving.....the meat fell of of the bone and were the hit of the party.

I registered just to say a big thank you to the person who posted this.  Cooking the ribs at 300 degrees in the tin foil is such an easy trick to reproduce that restaurant quality fall-off-the-bone tenderness that even I couldn't screw it up!  I pulled off the membrane on my ribs and basted both sides with bbq sauce.  I completely skipped the marination step so the tenderness of the meat is really due the cooking style.  Like others, I broiled the ribs meat side up with extra sauce on top after the ribs finished baking in the oven.  Thanks a million!

text:
This was my first attempt at making bbq ribs, as I always thought they would be to time consuming to make as many recipes say to boil the ribs. These were so EASY EASY EASY!! The only thing I put on them was a no name barbeque sauce from my local supermarket and marinated the ribs for 3 hours (as it was a last minute idea). I put them right from the fridge into a roasting pan lined with tin foil (just in case they leaked a bit....which they did). Cooked them as suggested for 2 1/2 hours at 300degrees. The meat was so tender that it just fell off the bones!  My son couldn't beleive that Mom made them!! These were so YUMMY !!

text:
Wow!  Surprisingly good.  I used a reviewer's suggestion and marinated with a dry rub for 48 hours.  To cook, I wrapped them in the non-stick aluminum foil and added a little of our favorite BBQ sauce (Head Country original).  My family groaned about cooking the ribs in the oven until I told them I planned to "finish" them on the grill.  That did the trick.  The ribs were already quite tender from slow cooking in the oven, but 10 minutes on the grill while basting with more BBQ sauce made them just slightly crisp on the outside and tangy from the BBQ sauce.  I will make them again!  Oh, and they're great with the Roasted Red New Potatoes...recipe found here on allrecipes.com.

text:
I made 2 full racks of ribs, cut each rack in half, basted with BBQ sauce, placed them in foil pouches and let them marinate overnight in the fridge.  I then baked them in a 300 oven for 2 hours.  The foil pouches puffed up nicely while they were cooking.  I removed the ribs, basted with more BBQ sauce and then refrigerated overnight.  The next evening my husband grilled them over coals for about 10 minutes to heat them and crisp them up on the outside.  He basted with more sauce too.  Everyone loved them!  My 13 year old son raved that this was his new favorite meal.  The meat in my opinion was a little dry, I would have like them to be a bit juicier, but the flavor was terrific, and pre-cooking them in the oven made them very tender.  The meat came off the bone very easily but didnt fall off the bones so it was just right.  Next time I make these I think I will bake them for 2 hours at 200 instead of 300.  Hopefully they will be a bit moister on the inside next time.  Overall they were OUTSTANDING!  Just have to figure out how to keep them a little moister.  Im open for suggestions.

text:
All I have to say is DELICIOUS!  This is also so simple.  I followed the advice of one reviewer and rubbed the ribs with cajun spices first and put everything in a slow cooker for a few hours.  I had tried bbq ribs before (on the grill), but they have never been as tender as this!  Next time, I will try to find a homemade bbq sauce to see if it makes the recipe even better!

Delicious!  I made the recipe even easier by eliminating the tin foil.  I rubbed the ribs down with my favorite cajun spice mix, salt and pepper.  Then I placed them directly in the slow cooker and coated them with BBQ sauce and cooked on low all day.  They were fabulous!  The cooker pot was no problem to clean either.
